   }\n369\t\n370\t    pub fn finding(&self) -> Option<ValidationFinding> {\n371\t        match self.record.kind {\n372\t            RecordKind::AddressV4\n373\t                if self\n374\t                    .record\n375\t                    .value\n376\t                    .as_str()\n377\t                    .parse::<std::net::Ipv4Addr>()\n378\t                    .is_err() =>\n379\t            {\n380\t                Some(self.finding_with_message(\"A record value must be an IPv4 address\"))\n381\t            }\n382\t            RecordKind::AddressV6\n383\t                if self\n384\t                    .record\n385\t                    .value\n386\t                    .as_str()\n387\t                    .parse::<std::net::Ipv6Addr>()\n388\t                    .is_err() =>\n389\t            {\n390\t                Some(self.finding_with_message(\"AAAA record value must be an IPv6 address\"))\n391\t            }\n392\t            RecordKind::CanonicalName\n393\t            | {\n398\t                Some(self.finding_with_message(\"record target must not be empty\"))\n399\t            }\n400\t            _ => None,\n401\t        }\n402\t    }\n403\t\n404\t    fn          \"{} {:?}: {}\",\n409\t                self.record.name.as_str(),\n410\t                self.record.kind,\n411\t                message\n412\t            ),\n413\t        }\n414\t    }\n415\t}\n416\t\n417\tpub struct RedirectValidation<'redirect> {\n418\t    redirect: &'redirect signal_cloud::RedirectRule,\n419\t}\n420\t\n421\timpl<'redirect> RedirectValidation<'redirect> {\n422\t    pub fn new(redirect: &'redirect signal_cloud::RedirectRule) -> Self {\n423\t        Self { redirect }\n424\t    }\n425\t\n426\t    pub fn finding(&self) -> Option<ValidationFinding> {\n427\t Eq)]\n443\tpub struct RecordPlan {\n444\t    current: Vec<DomainNameSystemRecord>,\n445\t    desired: Vec<DomainNameSystemRecord>,\n446\t}\n447\t\n448\timpl RecordPlan {\n449\t    pub fn new(current: Vec<DomainNameSystemRecord>, desired: Vec<DomainNameSystemRecord>) -> Self {\n450\t        Self { current, desired }\n451\t    }\n452\t\n453\t    pub fn into_parts(self) -> RecordPlanParts {\n454\t        let records_to_create = self\n455\t            .desired\n456\t            .iter()\n457\t            .filter(|desired| {\n458\t                !self\n459\t                    .current\n460\t                    .iter()\n461\t                    .any(|current| self.same_identity(current, desired))\n462\t            })\n463\t            .cloned()\n464\t            .collect();\n465\t        let           .any(|current| self.same_identity(current, desired) && current != *desired)\n472\t            })\n473\t            .cloned()\n474\t            .collect();\n475\t        let mut record_names_to_delete = Vec::new();\n476\t        for current in self.current.iter().filter(|current| {\n477\t            !self\n478\t                .desired\n479\t                .iter()\n480\t                .any(|desired| self.same_identity(current, desired))\n481\t        }) {\n482\t            if !record_names_to_delete.contains(&current.name) {\n483\t                record_names_to_delete.push(current.name.clone());\n484\t            }\n485\t        }\n486\t        RecordPlanParts {\n487\t            records_to_create,\n488\t            records_to_update,\n489\t            record_names_to_delete,\n490\t        }\n491\t    }\n492\t\n493\t    fn same_identity(&self, left: &DomainNameSystemRecord, right: &DomainNameSystemRecord) -> bool {\n494\t        left.name == right.name && left.kind == right.kind\n495\t    }\n496\t}\n497\t\n498\t#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]\n499\tpub struct RecordPlanParts {\n500\t    pub records_to_create:           CloudOperation::Validate(validation) => self.validate(validation.desired_state),\n648\t        }\n649\t    }\n650\t\n651\t    fn observe(&self, observation: Observation) -> CloudReply {\n652\t        match observation {\n653\t            Observation::Capabilities(query) => {\n654\t                CloudReply::Observed(ObservationResult::Capabilities(self.capabilities(query)))\n655\t            }\n656\t            Observation::Zones(query) => self.observe_zones(query),\n657\t            Observation::Records(query) => self.observe_records(query),\n658\t            Observation::Redirects(query) => {\n659\t                if let Some(reply) =\n660\t                    self.unsupported_provider_reply(query.provider, Some(Capability::RedirectRules))\n661\t                {\n662\t                    return reply;\n663\t                }\n664\t                if !Self::provider_supports_capability(query.provider, Capability::RedirectRules) {\n665\t !self.provider_is_configured(query.provider) {\n672\t                    return CloudReply::RequestUnsupported(RequestUnsupported {\n673\t                        provider: Some(query.provider),\n674\t                        capability: Some(Capability::RedirectRules),\n675\t                        reason: UnsupportedReason::ProviderNotConfigured,\n676\t                    });\n677\t                }\n678\t                CloudReply::RequestUnsupported(RequestUnsupported {\n679\t                    provider: Some(query.provider),\n680\t                    capability: Some(Capability::RedirectRules),\n681\t                    reason: UnsupportedReason::CapabilityNotCompiled,\n682\t                })\n683\t            }\n684\t            Observation::Plan(query) => (Provider::Cloudflare, Capability::DomainNameSystemRecords),\n691\t            (Provider::Cloudflare, Capability::RedirectRules),\n692\t            (Provider::GoogleCloud, query\n701\t                .provider\n702\t                .is_none_or(|requested| requested == *provider)\n703\t                && query\n704\t                    .capability\n705\t                    .is_none_or(|requested| requested == *capability)\n706\t        })\n707\t        .map(|(provider, capability)| CapabilityObservation {\n708\t            provider,\n709\t  fn observe_zones(&self, query: ZoneQuery) -> CloudReply {\n717\t        if let Some(provider) = query.provider {\n718\t            if let Some(reply) =\n719\t                self.unsupported_provider_reply(provider, Some(Capability::DomainNameSystemRecords))\n720\t            {\n721\t                return reply;\n722\t            }\n723\t            if }\n735\t        CloudReply::Observed(ObservationResult::Zones(self.zones()))\n736\t    }\n737\t\n738\t    fn observe_records(&self, query: RecordQuery) -> CloudReply {\n739\t        if let Some(reply)       }\n759\t        #[cfg(feature = \"cloudflare\")]\n760\t        if query.provider == Provider::Cloudflare {\n761\t            return self.observe_cloudflare_records(query);\n762\t        }\n763\t        CloudReply::Observed(ObservationResult::Records(RecordListing {\n764\t            records: vec![],\n765\t        }))\n766\t    }\n767\t\n768\t    fn zones(&self) -> ZoneListing {\n769\t zone_policy in &policy.zones {\n773\t            if !Self::provider_is_built(zone_policy.provider) {\n774\t                continue;\n775\t            }\n776\t            if !accounts.iter().any(|account| {\n777\t                account.provider == zone_policy.provider && account.account == zone_policy.account\n778\t            }) {\n779\t                continue;\n780\t            }\n781\t            for domain in &zone_policy.allowed_zones {\n782\t                zones.push(Zone {\n783\t                    provider: zone_policy.provider,\n784\t                    account: zone_policy.account.clone(),\n785\t                    identifier: signal_cloud::ZoneIdentifier::new(format!(\n786\t                        \"{}:{}\",\n787\t                        zone_policy.account.as_str(),\n788\t                        domain.as_str()\n789\t                    )),\n790\t                    name: domain.clone(),\n791\t                });\n792\t            }\n793\t        }\n794\t        ZoneListing { zones }\n795\t    }\n796\t\n797\t    pub fn last_known_records(\n798\t        &self,\n799\t        provider: Provider,\n800\t        zone: .iter()\n806\t            .find(|listing| listing.provider == provider && &listing.zone == zone)\n807\t            .map(|listing| listing.listing.clone())\n808\t    }\n809\t\n810\t    pub fn .expect(\"last known zones mutex\")\n816\t                .clone(),\n817\t        }\n818\t    }\n819\t\n820\t    #[cfg(feature = \"cloudflare\")]\n821\t    fn observe_cloudflare_zones(\n822\t   }),\n854\t        }\n855\t    }\n856\t\n857\t    #[cfg(feature = \"cloudflare\")]\n858\t    fn cloudflare_zone_listing(\n859\t        &self,\n860\t        account:    fn account_bindings(\n909\t        &self,\n910\t        provider: Provider,\n911\t        account: Option<meta_signal_cloud::ProviderAccount>,\n912\t    ) -> Vec<AccountBinding> {\n913\t This retires the prior hand-written `SchemaDaemon` / `CloudRuntime` /\n15\t//! `serve_*` / `ListenerRole` plumbing into the emitted output (report 542 /\n16\t//! Spirit ocu7): cloud is the first multi-listener triad_main pilot and the\n17\t//! first whose working contract is a dependency crate (`signal-cloud`).\n18\t\n19\tuse std::sync::Arc;\n20\tuse std::time::Duration;\n21\t\n22\tuse signal_cloud::schema::lib::{Input, Output};\n23\tuse tokio::io::AsyncWriteExt;\n24\tuse triad_runtime::{\n25\t    AcceptedConnection, ConnectionContext, FrameBody, LengthPrefixedCodec, MaximumFrameLength,\n26\t};\n27\t\n28\tuse crate::schema::daemon::{ComponentDaemon, DaemonBinder, DaemonError};\n29\tuse crate::{DaemonConfiguration, Error, Result, Store};\n30\t\n31\t/// Maximum inbound meta-request-frame body the daemon accepts (8 MiB). A cloud\n32\t/// request is a few hundred bytes; this bounds a hostile length prefix far below\n33\t/// the 4 GiB the u32-prefix codec default would pre-allocate. The working tier's\n34\t/// frame bound is the emitted spine's concern; this guards the component-owned\n35\t/// meta escape hatch.\n36\tconst MAXIMUM_REQUEST_FRAME_BYTES: usize = 8 * 1024 * 1024;\n37\t\n38\t/// How long the meta handler waits for a connected client to send its request\n39\t/// frame before dropping the stream. A legitimate client sends immediately.\n40\tconst REQUEST_READ_TIMEOUT: Duration = Duration::from_secs(10);\n41\t\n42\t/// The type-level selector for cloud's emitted daemon. It carries no runtime\n43\t/// data — it is the marker the emitted `DaemonCommand<CloudDaemon>` and the\n44\t/// generated runtime dispatch on, selecting cloud's `Configuration` / `Engine`\n45\t/// / `Error` through the `ComponentDaemon` associated types.\n46\tpub struct CloudDaemon;\n47\t\n48\timpl ComponentDaemon for CloudDaemon {\n49\t    type Configuration = DaemonConfiguration;\n50\t    type ConfigurationError = Error;\n51\t    /// The engine is the shared provider store. The actor-native listener owns\n52\t    /// the socket/connection lifecycle; cloud keeps the provider behavior in\n53\t    /// the existing store until the schema effect plane carries provider IO.\n54\t    type Engine = Arc<Store>;\n55\t    type Error = Error;\n56\t\n57\t    const PROCESS_NAME: &'static str = \"cloud-daemon\";\n58\t\n59\t    fn load_configuration(\n60\t        path: &std::path::Path,\n61\t    ) -> std::result::Result<Self::Configuration, Self::ConfigurationError> {\n62\t        let bytes = std::fs::read(path)?;\n63\t        DaemonConfiguration::from_rkyv_bytes(&bytes)\n64\t    }\n65\t\n66\t    fn build_runtime(_configuration: &Self::Configuration) -> Result<Self::Engine> {\n67\t        Ok(Arc::new(Store::new()))\n68\t    }\n69\t\n70\t    /// Run one decoded ordinary `Input` through the shared provider store and\n71\t    /// return the ordinary `Output`. The schema bridge preserves today's\n72\t    /// provider behavior while the effect plane catches up; cloud does not\n73\t    /// classify by origin yet, so the peer-credential `connection` is unused.\n74\t    async fn handle_working_input(\n75\t        engine: &mut Self::Engine,\n76\t        input: Input,\n77\t        _connection: &ConnectionContext,\n78\t    ) -> Result<Output> {\n79\t        Ok(engine.handle_schema_ordinary_input(input))\n80\t    }\n81\t\n82\t    /// Serve one meta request end to end: decode a meta-signal-cloud\n83\t    /// `Input` off the length-prefixed frame, drive it through a per-request\n84\t    /// engine, and write the meta `Output` back. The meta wire codec is\n85\t    /// component-owned (the emitter routes the meta socket here rather than\n86\t    /// emitting a second frame spine), so this owns the full read/handle/write.\n87\t    async fn handle_meta_connection(\n88\t        engine: &mut Self::Engine,\n89\t        mut connection: AcceptedConnection,\n90\t    ) -> Result<()> {\n91\t        let codec = LengthPrefixedCodec::new(MaximumFrameLength::new(MAXIMUM_REQUEST_FRAME_BYTES));\n92\t        let body = tokio::time::timeout(\n93\t            REQUEST_READ_TIMEOUT,\n94\t            codec.read_body_async(connection.stream_mut()),\n95\t        )\n96\t        .await\n97\t        .map_err(|_| Error::RequestReadTimedOut)??;\n98\t        let (_route, input) =\n99\t            meta_signal_cloud::schema::lib::Input::decode_signal_frame(body.bytes())?;\n100\t        let reply = engine.handle_schema_meta_input(input);\n101\t        codec\n102\t            .write_body_async(\n103\t                connection.stream_mut(),\n104\t                &FrameBody::new(reply.encode_signal_frame()?),\n105\t            )\n106\t            .await?;\n107\t        connection.stream_mut().flush().await?;\n108\t        Ok(())\n109\t    }\n110\t}\n111\t\n112\t/// A thin convenience wrapper so in-process launchers and tests keep the\n113\t/// familiar `SchemaDaemon::new(configuration).run()` surface over the emitted\n114\t/// `ComponentDaemon` binder. The bin uses the emitted `DaemonEntry` directly.\n115\tpub struct SchemaDaemon {\n116\t    configuration: DaemonConfiguration,\n117\t}\n118\t\n119\timpl SchemaDaemon {\n120\t    pub fn new(configuration: DaemonConfiguration) -> Self {\n121\t        Self { configuration }\n122\t    }\n123\t\n124\t    pub fn run(self) -> std::result::Result<(), DaemonError<CloudDaemon>> {\n125\t        tokio::runtime::Runtime::new()\n126\t            .map_err(DaemonError::Runtime)?\n127\t            .block_on(async {\n128\t                CloudDaemon::bind(self.configuration)?\n129\t                    .run()\n130\t                    .await\n131\t                    .map_err(DaemonError::from)\n132\t            })\n133\t    }\n134\t}\n135\t"}]},"uuid":"5b83ac3b-a276-40e0-90ee-49653074ffcc","timestamp":"2026-06-17T17:06:04.511Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"5af61d90-5bf1-4996-9160-381f5f795b20","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/li/primary","sessionId":"bb3c1115-0b29-4b2b-8843-15cbe1850dfc","version":"2.1.170","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"mutable-foraging-sparkle"}

The signal-cloud crate has BOTH a hand-written `src/lib.rs` (public legacy API consumed by `cloud`) AND a generated `src/schema/lib.rs` (the wire codec, from `schema/lib.schema`). Both must change in lockstep when adding wire variants. The `cloud` crate depends on the sibling crates via git `branch = \"main\"` with no `[patch]`, so the implementer must push the sibling schema changes (or add a `[patch.crates-io]`/git path override) before `cloud` can consume them.\n\nI now have a complete, code-anchored understanding. Here is the spec.\n\n---\n\n# Implementation Spec: Hetzner Compute Provider (Phase 1) for the `cloud` daemon\n\n## 0. Architectural ground truth (read this first — it reshapes the plan)\n\nThere are **two parallel engines** in this repo and they are NOT interchangeable:\n\n1. **The LIVE daemon path** — the provider `Store` in `/git/github.com/LiGoldragon/cloud/src/lib.rs`. This is what `cloud-daemon` actually runs (`schema_daemon.rs:66-68` builds `Arc::new(Store::new())` as the `Engine`; `schema_daemon.rs:74-80` routes `handle_working_input` → `Store::handle_schema_ordinary_input`; `:87-109` routes meta → `Store::handle_schema_meta_input`). The Cloudflare provider lives here, synchronously (`lib.rs:1240-1262` `apply_cloudflare_plan` → `cloudflare.rs` blocking `ureq`).\n\n2. **The SCHEMA-ENGINE path** — `SchemaRuntime` in `src/schema_runtime.rs` with the Nexus/Sema/Effect planes (`schema/nexus.schema`, `schema/sema.schema`). This is explicitly described as \"still the pure schema/Nexus/SEMA experiment\" (`schema_runtime.rs:12-14`) and the live daemon does NOT use it. Its `EffectCommand`/`EffectResult` (`nexus.schema:40-46`, `run_effect` at `schema_runtime.rs:497-509`) return empty stubs.\n\n**Decision:** Phase 1 Hetzner mirrors **Cloudflare-in-the-`Store`** (path 1), because that is the shipped path. Do **not** wire Hetzner into `SchemaRuntime::run_effect` for Phase 1 — that engine isn't reachable from `cloud-daemon`. (The nexus `EffectCommand` plane is, however, the right *eventual* home for deferral; see §6.)\n\nA second hard constraint: the wire contracts (`Provider`, `Capability`, `Observation`, `DesiredState`, `Plan`, the Mutate ops) live in **separate git crates** — `signal-cloud` and `meta-signal-cloud` — pulled by `branch = \"main\"` (`Cargo.toml:35,37`), with **no `[patch]`**. Each has a **hand-written `src/lib.rs` (legacy public API)** AND a **generated `src/schema/lib.rs` (wire codec from `schema/lib.schema`)** that must change in lockstep, plus the `cloud`-side `schema_bridge.rs` that maps between them. So any new wire record is a **3-repo change**, gated behind pushing the sibling crates first.\n\n**Good news the audit didn't flag:** `Provider::Hetzner` and `Capability::{CloudHosts,Networks,Firewalls,LoadBalancers}` **already exist** in both wire schemas (`signal-cloud/schema/lib.schema:23-24`, `meta-signal-cloud/schema/lib.schema:76-77`), in the generated Rust, in the legacy Rust (`signal-cloud/src/lib.rs:62,81,112,114`), and in the bridge (`schema_bridge.rs:293,357-361`). The capability matrix in `lib.rs:688-714` and `:1354-1363` already lists all four Hetzner capabilities. So provider/capability identity is done; what's missing is (a) the `hetzner` feature being empty, (b) no `hetzner.rs` adapter, (c) no `CloudHost`/`DesiredHostState`/`HostPlan` records on the wire, and (d) no host create/observe/destroy handlers in the `Store`.\n\n---\n\n## 1. add `Servers` arm to `Observation` + `ObservationResult` | `Zone`/`ZoneListing`/`ZoneQuery` at `:34-36`, `Zones` arm at `:47,49,53` |\n| 2 | `signal-cloud/src/lib.rs` | Hand-add the same `CloudHost`/`CloudHostListing`/`HostQuery` structs + `Observation::Servers`/`ObservationResult::Servers` + `ObservationKind::Servers` | `Zone` struct + `Observation` enum at `:338-388` |\n| 3 | `signal-cloud/src/schema/lib.rs` | **Regenerate** via `SIGNAL_CLOUD_UPDATE_SCHEMA_ARTIFACTS=1 cargo build` (do not hand-edit) | generated `Zones(Zones)` plumbing |\n| 4 | `meta-signal-cloud/schema/lib.schema` | Add `DesiredHostState` record, `HostPlan` record; add to `[dependencies]` as optional | `cloudflare = [\"dep:serde\", \"dep:serde_json\", \"dep:ureq\"]` at `:28` |\n| 7 | `cloud/src/hetzner.rs` | **NEW** — `Api` trait + `HttpApi` + `ProviderClient` + `EnvironmentCredentialSource` reuse | entire `cloudflare.rs` |\n| 8 | `cloud/src/lib.rs` | `mod hetzner` decl; `Store.hetzner` field; `Store::new`/`with_parts` cfg arms; host observe handler; host plan prepare/apply; `apply_plan` provider match arm; error mapper | `cloudflare` field `:530-531`, `with_parts` `:567-594`, `observe_cloudflare_*` `:840-887`, `apply_cloudflare_plan` `:1240-1262`, `meta_reply_for_cloudflare_error` `:1271-1287` |\n| 9 | `cloud/src/schema_bridge.rs` | Add `CloudHost`/`Servers` Legacy↔Schema mappers; extend `SchemaObservation`/`LegacyObservation` + `*ObservationResult` match arms | `SchemaObservation` `:466-497`, `LegacyObservation` `:500-530`, `*ObservationResult` `:782-852` |\n| 10 | `cloud/flake.nix` | Add `hetznerCli`/token shim; add to `cloudRuntimePath` | `cloudflareCli` `:49-57`, `cloudRuntimePath` `:58` |\n| 11 | `cloud/src/lib.rs` `Error` enum | Add `#[cfg(feature=\"hetzner\")] Hetzner(#[from] hetzner::Error)` | `Cloudflare` variant `:117-119` |\n\n**Deferral seam (§6)** is a separate, smaller change set inside `Store` + a background executor; it does NOT require the schema crates.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Wire-schema snippets to ADD\n\n### 2a. `signal-cloud/schema/lib.schema`\n\nThe real syntax I'm mirroring (verbatim from `:34-36, :43, :45, :47-54`):\n```\nZoneQuery { provider (Optional Provider) account (Optional ProviderAccount) }\nZone { provider Provider provider_account ProviderAccount zone_identifier ZoneIdentifier domain_name DomainName }\nZoneListing { zones (Vector Zone) }\n...\nObservation [(Capabilities Capabilities) (Zones Zones) (Records Records) (Redirects Redirects) (ObservePlan ObservePlan)]\nZones ZoneQuery\nObservationResult [(Capabilities CapabilityReport) (Zones ZoneListing) (Records RecordListing) (Redirects RedirectListing) (PlanResult PlanResult)]\n```\n\nADD these lines (a `HostIdentifier` String alias near the other String aliases at `:16-22`, the records near `Zone`, and the `Servers` arms):\n```\n  HostIdentifier String\n  ServerType String\n  ImageName String\n  IpAddress String\n\n  HostQuery { provider Provider provider_account (Optional ProviderAccount) }\n  CloudHost { provider Provider provider_account ProviderAccount host_identifier HostIdentifier host_name DomainName server_type ServerType image_name ImageName ipv4_address IpAddress host_status HostStatus }\n  HostStatus [Initializing Running Stopped Deleting Unknown]\n  CloudHostListing { hosts (Vector CloudHost) }\n```\nThen EXTEND the two existing roots — add the `Servers` arm to each (note: variant-name `Servers`, payload-type names must be distinct constructor types like the existing `Zones`/`Records` pattern, so introduce `ObserveServers HostQuery`):\n```\n  Observation [(Capabilities Capabilities) (Zones Zones) (Records Records) (Redirects Redirects) (ObserveServers ObserveServers) (ObservePlan ObservePlan)]\n  ObserveServers HostQuery\n  ObservationResult [(Capabilities CapabilityReport) (Zones ZoneListing) (Records RecordListing) (Redirects RedirectListing) (Servers CloudHostListing) (PlanResult PlanResult)]\n```\n\n### 2b. `signal-cloud/src/lib.rs` (hand-written legacy mirror)\n\nMirror the `Zone` struct (`:35` schema / the generated counterpart) and the `Observation` enum (`:338-356`). ADD:\n```rust\n#[derive(Archive, RkyvSerialize, RkyvDeserialize, NotaEncode, NotaDecode, Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]\npub struct CloudHost {\n    pub provider: Provider,\n    pub account: ProviderAccount,\n    pub identifier: HostIdentifier,   // newtype String, mirror ZoneIdentifier\n    pub name: DomainName,\n    pub server_type: ServerType,\n    pub image: ImageName,\n    pub ipv4: IpAddress,\n    pub status: HostStatus,\n}\n// + CloudHostListing { hosts: Vec<CloudHost> }, HostQuery { provider, account: Option<_> }, HostStatus enum\n```\nand add `Servers(HostQuery)` to `Observation` (+ `ObservationKind::Servers` at `:371-377`) and `Servers(CloudHostListing)` to `ObservationResult` (`:382-388`).\n\n### 2c. `meta-signal-cloud/schema/lib.schema` — RECOMMENDED: a dedicated host plan, NOT a union\n\nThe real op + record syntax I'm mirroring (verbatim from `:5-9, :43, :50-66`):\n```\n (PreparePlan PlanPreparation)\n (ApprovePlan Approval)\n (ApplyPlan Application)\n...\nPlanPreparation DesiredState\nPlan { identifier PlanIdentifier provider Provider zone DomainName records_to_create (Vector DomainNameSystemRecord) ... }\nDesiredState { provider Provider zone DomainName records (Vector DomainNameSystemRecord) redirects (Vector RedirectRule) }\n```\n\n**Justification for a separate `HostPlan` rather than unioning into `Plan`:** `Plan`/`DesiredState` are keyed on a DNS `zone DomainName` and carry only record/redirect vectors. A host has no zone and a fundamentally different shape (server_type/image/ssh_key, a single create/destroy intent, no diff-of-vectors). Cramming nullable host fields into `Plan` would (a) force every existing Cloudflare codepath (`lib.rs:1071-1083`, `schema_bridge.rs:LegacyPlan`) to thread empty host fields, and (b) break the `RecordPlan` diff semantics (`lib.rs:448-503`) which assume name+kind identity. A parallel `HostPlan` + `ApprovePlan`/`ApplyPlan` reuse (plans are addressed by `PlanIdentifier` String — `:45-46` — so approve/apply already work on any plan id) is the minimal, clean addition.\n\nADD to `meta-signal-cloud/schema/lib.schema`:\n```\n  ServerType String\n  ImageName String\n  SshKeyName String\n\n  DesiredHostState { provider Provider host_name DomainName server_type ServerType image_name ImageName ssh_key_name SshKeyName }\n  HostPlan {\n    identifier PlanIdentifier\n    provider Provider\n    host_name DomainName\n    server_type ServerType\n    image_name ImageName\n    ssh_key_name SshKeyName\n    intent HostIntent\n  }\n  HostIntent [Create Destroy]\n```\nAdd ONE new mutate op (prepare); reuse existing `ApprovePlan`/`ApplyPlan` (they take `PlanIdentifier`, so no new approve/apply op is needed — this is the key economy). Extend the input root list (`:2-9`) and the dispatch:\n```\n (PrepareHostPlan PrepareHostPlan)\n...\n  PrepareHostPlan DesiredHostState\n```\nAnd add a reply arm to the output root (`:10-17`) — reuse `PlanPrepared` shape but for a host plan, OR add:\n```\n (HostPlanPrepared HostPlanPrepared)\n...\n  HostPlanPrepared HostPlan\n```\nMirror the same in `meta-signal-cloud/src/lib.rs` (hand) and regenerate `src/schema/lib.rs`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. `Cargo.toml` feature + deps\n\nCurrently `hetzner = []` (`Cargo.toml:30`). Mirror the cloudflare feature (`:28`). The cloudflare adapter uses **blocking `ureq`** (not async reqwest) precisely so the synchronous `Store` can call it. **Reuse the same stack** for Phase 1 consistency (reqwest async would force a runtime-block-in-actor, which is worse):\n\n```toml\n# [features]\nhetzner = [\"dep:serde\", \"dep:serde_json\", \"dep:ureq\"]\n```\nNo new `[dependencies]` lines are needed — `serde`, `serde_json`, `ureq` are already declared optional (`:40-41,45`). (If the implementer insists on `reqwest`, add `reqwest = { version = \"0.12\", default-features = false, features = [\"json\",\"blocking\",\"rustls-tls\"], optional = true }` and put it in the feature list — but the spec's recommendation is `ureq`, matching `cloudflare.rs:140-205`.)\n\nThe Hetzner token env var name: define `const TOKEN_ENVIRONMENT_VARIABLE: &str = \"HCLOUD_TOKEN\";` in `hetzner.rs` (mirrors `cloudflare_cli.rs:18` `CF_API_TOKEN`). The `CredentialHandle` registered via meta `RegisterAccount` carries the env-var name; `EnvironmentCredentialSource::token` (`cloudflare.rs:51-57`) reads `std::env::var(handle.as_str())` — reuse it verbatim.\n\n---\n\n## 4. `flake.nix` Hetzner gopass shim\n\nMirror `cloudflareCli` (`:49-57`) and `cloudRuntimePath` (`:58`). Hetzner has no first-party CLI that the daemon shells out to for create (we use the REST API in-process), so unlike `flarectl` the shim's only job is to **inject `HCLOUD_TOKEN` from gopass into the daemon's environment**. The daemon binary itself is wrapped (`:68-70`). Replace the `postInstall` wrap to also export the token, and keep the `hcloud` CLI on PATH for operator debugging:\n\nADD after `cloudflareCli` (`:57`):\n```nix\n        hetznerCli = pkgs.symlinkJoin {\n          name = \"hcloud-gopass-wrapped\";\n          paths = [ pkgs.hcloud ];\n          nativeBuildInputs = [ pkgs.makeWrapper ];\n          postBuild = ''\n            wrapProgram $out/bin/hcloud \\\n              --run 'HCLOUD_TOKEN=$(${pkgs.gopass}/bin/gopass show -o hetzner/api-token) || { echo \"cloud: cannot fetch HCLOUD_TOKEN from gopass hetzner/api-token\" >&2; exit 78; }; export HCLOUD_TOKEN'\n          '';\n        };\n```\nCHANGE `cloudRuntimePath` (`:58`) to include it:\n```nix\n        cloudRuntimePath = pkgs.lib.makeBinPath [ cloudflareCli hetznerCli ];\n```\nCHANGE the daemon `postInstall` wrap (`:68-70`) so the daemon process itself gets `HCLOUD_TOKEN` (the in-process REST call reads it via `EnvironmentCredentialSource`):\n```nix\n            postInstall = ''\n              wrapProgram $out/bin/cloud-daemon \\\n                --prefix PATH : ${cloudRuntimePath} \\\n                --run 'export HCLOUD_TOKEN=''${HCLOUD_TOKEN:-$(${pkgs.gopass}/bin/gopass show -o hetzner/api-token 2>/dev/null)}'\n            '';\n```\nAdd `hetznerCli` to `devShells.default.packages` (`:119-124`).\n\n---\n\n## 5. `src/hetzner.rs` skeleton\n\nMirror `cloudflare.rs` structurally: `Error`/`Result` (`cloudflare.rs:11-29`), `Token` (`:31-42`), `CredentialSource`+`EnvironmentCredentialSource` (`:44-57` — can be re-exported from `cloudflare` instead of duplicated, but Phase 1 keeps it local for feature independence), `trait Api` (`:59-81`), `HttpApi` with `get/post/delete` (`:111-217`), `ProviderClient` (`:283-423`). Hetzner's REST envelope differs from Cloudflare's `{success,result,errors}` (`:435-456`): Hetzner returns `{server:{...}}` / `{servers:[...]}` / `{action:{...}}` and errors as HTTP status + `{error:{code,message}}`, so `decode_response` is simpler (no success flag; check HTTP status).\n\n```rust\n//! Hetzner Cloud compute provider adapter (HTTP, blocking ureq).\n//! Mirrors src/cloudflare.rs: trait Api + HttpApi + ProviderClient.\n\nuse std::fmt;\nuse std::sync::Arc;\n\nuse meta_signal_cloud::CredentialHandle;\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse signal_cloud::{CloudHost, DomainName, HostStatus, Provider, ProviderAccount};\n\n#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)]\npub enum Error {\n    #[error(\"credential handle is not available in the environment: {0}\")]\n    CredentialUnavailable(String),\n    #[error(\"Hetzner request failed: {0}\")]\n    RequestFailed(String),\n    #[error(\"Hetzner rejected request: {0}\")]\n    RequestRejected(String),\n    #[error(\"Hetzner host was not found: {0}\")]\n    HostNotFound(String),\n}\npub type Result<T> = std::result::Result<T, Error>;\n\n// Token + CredentialSource + EnvironmentCredentialSource: copy cloudflare.rs:31-57 verbatim.\n\n// ---- domain newtypes (mirror cloudflare::RecordIdentifier:90-100) ----\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]\npub struct HostIdentifier(String); // impl new/as_str\n\n// ---- the engine trait (mirror cloudflare.rs:59-81) ----\npub trait Api: Send + Sync {\n    fn ensure_ssh_key(&self, token: &Token, name: &str, public_key: &str) -> Result<i64>;\n    fn create_server(&self, token: &Token, spec: &ServerSpec) -> Result<ApiServer>;\n    fn get_server(&self, token: &Token, id: &HostIdentifier) -> Result<ApiServer>;\n    fn list_servers(&self, token: &Token) -> Result<Vec<ApiServer>>;\n    fn delete_server(&self, token: &Token, id: &HostIdentifier) -> Result<()>;\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct ServerSpec {\n    pub name: String,\n    pub server_type: String,   // e.g. \"cx22\"\n    pub image: String,         // e.g. \"debian-12\"\n    pub ssh_key_ids: Vec<i64>,\n    pub location: Option<String>,\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]\npub struct ApiServer {\n    pub identifier: HostIdentifier,\n    pub name: DomainName,\n    pub server_type: String,\n    pub image: String,\n    pub ipv4: String,\n    pub status: HostStatus,\n}\n\n// ---- HttpApi (mirror cloudflare.rs:111-223) ----\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct HttpApi { base_url: String }\n\nimpl HttpApi {\n    pub fn new() -> Self { Self { base_url: \"https://api.hetzner.cloud\".to_owned() } }\n    // get/post/delete: copy cloudflare.rs:129-206 but:\n    //   - no Envelope; decode the typed body directly.\n    //   - on non-2xx, ureq returns Err(ureq::Error::Status(code, resp)); map to RequestRejected\n    //     by reading resp.into_string() (Hetzner JSON {error:{message}}).\n}\n\nimpl Api for HttpApi {\n    fn ensure_ssh_key(&self, token: &Token, name: &str, public_key: &str) -> Result<i64> {\n        // GET /v1/ssh_keys?name={name}; if present return id.\n        // else POST /v1/ssh_keys  body {\"name\":name,\"public_key\":public_key} -> {ssh_key:{id}}\n    }\n    fn create_server(&self, token: &Token, spec: &ServerSpec) -> Result<ApiServer> {\n        // POST /v1/servers\n        //   body: {\"name\":..,\"server_type\":..,\"image\":..,\"ssh_keys\":[id..],\"location\":..,\"start_after_create\":true}\n        //   -> {\"server\":{id,name,status,public_net:{ipv4:{ip}},server_type:{name},image:{name}}, \"action\":{...}}\n        // map server.status string -> HostStatus (initializing|running|... -> enum)\n    }\n    fn get_server(&self, token: &Token, id: &HostIdentifier) -> Result<ApiServer> {\n        // GET /v1/servers/{id} -> {\"server\":{...}} ; 404 -> HostNotFound\n    }\n    fn list_servers(&self, token: &Token) -> Result<Vec<ApiServer>> {\n        // GET /v1/servers -> {\"servers\":[...]}\n    }\n    fn delete_server(&self, token: &Token, id: &HostIdentifier) -> Result<()> {\n        // DELETE /v1/servers/{id} -> {\"action\":{...}} ; treat 404 as already-gone Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n// ---- ProviderClient (mirror cloudflare.rs:283-423) ----\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct ProviderClient {\n    api: Arc<dyn Api>,\n    credentials: Arc<dyn CredentialSource>,\n}\n\nimpl ProviderClient {\n    pub fn production() -> Self {\n        Self::new(Arc::new(HttpApi::new()), Arc::new(EnvironmentCredentialSource))\n    }\n    pub fn new(api: Arc<dyn Api>, credentials: Arc<dyn CredentialSource>) -> Self { Self { api, credentials } }\n\n    // mirror cloudflare.rs:308-310\n    pub fn verify_credential(&self, c: &CredentialHandle) -> Result<()> {\n        self.credentials.token(c).map(|_| ())\n    }\n\n    pub fn create_host(&self, c: &CredentialHandle, account: &ProviderAccount, spec: &ServerSpec) -> Result<CloudHost> {\n        let token = self.credentials.token(c)?;\n        let server = self.api.create_server(&token, spec)?;\n        Ok(into_cloud_host(Provider::Hetzner, account.clone(), server))\n    }\n    pub fn observe_hosts(&self, c: &CredentialHandle, account: &ProviderAccount) -> Result<Vec<CloudHost>> {\n        let token = self.credentials.token(c)?;\n        Ok(self.api.list_servers(&token)?.into_iter()\n            .map(|s| into_cloud_host(Provider::Hetzner, account.clone(), s)).collect())\n    }\n    pub fn destroy_host(&self, c: &CredentialHandle, id: &HostIdentifier) -> Result<()> {\n        let token = self.credentials.token(c)?;\n        self.api.delete_server(&token, id)\n    }\n}\n\n// impl fmt::Debug for ProviderClient: copy cloudflare.rs:425-433 (opaque fields).\n```\nRequest/response structs (`serde`): mirror `cloudflare.rs:463-534`. Concrete shapes:\n- `POST /v1/servers` request: `{ \"name\": String, \"server_type\": String, \"image\": String, \"ssh_keys\": Vec<i64>, \"start_after_create\": true, \"location\": Option<String> }`\n- create/get response: `struct ServerEnvelope { server: ServerRecord }`, `struct ServerRecord { id: i64, name: String, status: String, public_net: PublicNet, server_type: ServerTypeRef, image: Option<ImageRef> }`, `struct PublicNet { ipv4: Option<Ipv4Ref> }`, `struct Ipv4Ref { ip: String }`.\n- `GET /v1/servers` response: `struct ServersEnvelope { servers: Vec<ServerRecord> }`.\n- ssh_keys: `struct SshKeysEnvelope { ssh_keys: Vec<SshKeyRecord> }`, `struct SshKeyRecord { id: i64, name: String }`, create response `struct SshKeyEnvelope { ssh_key: SshKeyRecord }`.\n\nAuth header: `Authorization: Bearer {token}` — identical to `cloudflare.rs:139,163`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Where the REST call lives + the deferred-effect mechanism (the audit's core concern)\n\n### The blocking site, exactly\n\n`cloud-daemon` runs the emitted `GeneratedDaemonRuntime` (`src/schema/daemon.rs`). Every request is funneled through a **single kameo actor** `EngineActor` whose mailbox serializes all messages:\n- working: `src/schema/daemon.rs:340` `self.engine.ask(WorkingInput{..}).await` → handler at `:268-278` calls `Daemon::handle_working_input(&mut self.engine, ...)` with **exclusive `&mut`**.\n- meta: `:352` `self.engine.ask(MetaConnection{..}).await` → handler at `:284-293` calls `Daemon::handle_meta_connection(&mut self.engine, ...)`.\n\n`handle_meta_connection` (`schema_daemon.rs:87-109`) calls `engine.handle_schema_meta_input` synchronously → `Store::apply_plan` → (today) `apply_cloudflare_plan` → blocking `ureq`. **While that runs, the actor mailbox is blocked — no other ordinary or meta request is processed.** A Hetzner `create_server` (+ future install) can take tens of seconds. So a synchronous Hetzner apply would freeze the whole daemon. **The audit is correct.**\n\nNote the doc comment at `schema_daemon.rs:53-54` already concedes this: \"cloud keeps the provider behavior in the existing store until the schema effect plane carries provider IO.\" The Effect plane (`nexus.schema:40-46`) is the *intended* deferral home but is not wired into the live daemon.\n\n### Recommended minimal seam (no kameo internals, no schema-engine rewrite)\n\nThere is **no existing clean deferral seam** in the `Store` — every handler returns its terminal reply inline. Build the minimal one:\n\n**(a) Make the long apply return immediately with a deferred identifier.** In `Store`, add an in-memory job registry:\n```rust\n// in Store (lib.rs:522-532), behind #[cfg(feature=\"hetzner\")]\nhost_jobs: Mutex<Vec<HostJob>>,   // {id: PlanIdentifier, state: Pending|Running|Done(CloudHost)|Failed(reason)}\nhost_runtime: tokio::runtime::Handle,  // or a dedicated worker, see (b)\n```\n`apply_plan` (`lib.rs:1210`) for a host plan does **not** call `create_server` inline. It: validates approval (reuse `lib.rs:1216-1226`), inserts a `HostJob{state: Pending}`, **spawns the blocking call onto a separate thread/runtime** (see (b)), and returns `MetaReply::PlanApplied{plan}` immediately (the reply means \"accepted/started\", consistent with the existing `PlanApplied` semantics — the wire already has no synchronous \"Done\" guarantee). The operator then polls completion via a host observation (the new `Observation::Servers` arm), which reads provider state directly.\n\n**(b) Where the blocking call actually runs.** Two viable mechanisms; recommendation is the first for minimality:\n\n1. **`tokio::task::spawn_blocking` from inside the actor handler.** `handle_meta_connection` is already `async` on the tokio multi-thread runtime (`Cargo.toml:43` enables `rt-multi-thread`). Inside the host-apply branch, do:\n   ```rust\n   let client = self.hetzner.clone();          // ProviderClient is Clone (Arc inside)\n   let (cred, spec, jobs) = (...);             // cloned/Arc-shared\n   tokio::task::spawn_blocking(move || {\n       let result = client.create_host(&cred, &account, &spec);\n       // write result into the shared host_jobs Mutex\n   });\n   ```\n   This moves the blocking `ureq` call off the actor's poll thread onto tokio's blocking pool. The actor handler returns instantly; the mailbox unblocks. The job registry (an `Arc<Mutex<Vec<HostJob>>>` shared into the closure) carries the result back, observable via the Servers observation. **This is the minimal seam: ~no new dependency, no new actor, ~30 lines.** The one requirement: the `Store` must hand the closure an `Arc`-shareable handle to `host_jobs` (wrap that field in `Arc<Mutex<...>>` so it can be moved into `'static` closures).\n\n2. **A dedicated kameo worker actor** (heavier, the \"proper\" long-term shape). Spawn a second `HetznerWorker` kameo actor at `build_runtime` (`schema_daemon.rs:66`). The meta handler sends it a fire-and-forget `tell` (not `ask`) with the job; the worker processes one provision at a time off its own mailbox, writing results into the shared registry. This isolates provider IO from the engine mailbox entirely and gives natural backpressure/serialization of provisions. `kameo` is already in the tree (`Cargo.lock`), re-exported as `triad_runtime::kameo` (`daemon.rs:14-20`), so no new dep. Choose this only if Phase 2 (install/SSH orchestration) needs durable per-host actors.\n\n**Recommendation: ship (1) `spawn_blocking` + job registry for Phase 1.** It's the smallest change that satisfies \"long provider call must not block the listener,\" it requires zero schema-engine work, and the create/observe/destroy contract is fully expressible: create→deferred id, observe→poll real state, destroy→(fast enough to do inline, or same deferral).\n\n`reqwest` vs `ureq`: keep **blocking `ureq`** and run it under `spawn_blocking`. Async `reqwest` inside the actor would still need `.await` on the actor's single poll loop (blocking the mailbox during DNS/TLS/HTTP) unless also offloaded — so async buys nothing here and adds a dep. The REST call lives in `hetzner::HttpApi` (the sync engine trait `Api`), called from `ProviderClient`, invoked from the `spawn_blocking` closure — i.e. **off the listener thread, behind the `Store`, exactly parallel to where `cloudflare::HttpApi` sits today but offloaded.**\n\n---\n\n## 7. What BLOCKS this and must be built first\n\n1. **No deferral seam exists.** Every `Store` handler returns inline (`lib.rs:1124-1135` dispatch → each arm returns a terminal `MetaReply`). The `host_jobs` registry + `spawn_blocking` offload (§6b) **must be built before** any host apply, or the daemon freezes on every provision. This is the single hardest prerequisite; it is `cloud`-local (no schema crates).\n\n2. **The wire contract change is a 3-repo, push-gated change.** `cloud` consumes `signal-cloud`/`meta-signal-cloud` by `branch = \"main\"` with **no `[patch]`** (`Cargo.toml:35,37`; confirmed no patch section). Adding `CloudHost`/`Servers`/`DesiredHostState`/`HostPlan` requires editing **both** the schema file AND the hand-written `src/lib.rs` AND regenerating `src/schema/lib.rs` in each sibling repo, committing/pushing them, then bumping `cloud`'s lockfile. To iterate locally before pushing, the implementer must temporarily add to `cloud/Cargo.toml`:\n   ```toml\n   [patch.\"https://github.com/LiGoldragon/signal-cloud.git\"]\n   signal-cloud = { path = \"../../signal-cloud\" }\n   [patch.\"https://github.com/LiGoldragon/meta-signal-cloud.git\"]\n   meta-signal-cloud = { path = \"../../meta-signal-cloud\" }\n   ```\n   (local checkouts exist at `/git/github.com/LiGoldragon/signal-cloud` and `.../meta-signal-cloud`). This `[patch]` is itself a prerequisite for the dev loop.\n\n3. **Schema artifacts are checked-in and freshness-gated.** `build.rs` runs `write_or_check(\"CLOUD_UPDATE_SCHEMA_ARTIFACTS\")` and **fails the build if `src/schema/*.rs` is stale** (`build.rs` `.write_or_check(...)`). Same gate in the sibling crates (`META_SIGNAL_CLOUD_UPDATE_SCHEMA_ARTIFACTS`, `SIGNAL_CLOUD_UPDATE_SCHEMA_ARTIFACTS`). After any `.schema` edit, the implementer must run the build with the relevant `*_UPDATE_SCHEMA_ARTIFACTS=1` env var to regenerate, in each crate, or CI/`nix flake check` fails. **Order: sibling schema edit → regen sibling → regen `cloud` (nexus/sema unchanged for Phase 1) → build.**\n\n4. **`schema_bridge.rs` must grow new Legacy↔Schema arms or it won't compile.** `SchemaObservation::into_legacy` (`schema_bridge.rs:475-497`) and `LegacyObservation::into_schema` (`:509-529`) are exhaustive `match`es over the `Observation` enum; adding `Observation::Servers` to `signal-cloud` makes these non-exhaustive → compile error. Same for `ObservationResult` (`:791-852`). These arms (+ a `CloudHost`/`CloudHostListing` mapper pair mirroring `SchemaZoneListing`/`LegacyZoneListing` at `:903-960`) must be added in the same change as the schema edit.\n\n5. **No schema-engine effect work is needed or wanted for Phase 1** — but note `SchemaRuntime::run_effect` (`schema_runtime.rs:497-509`) and the nexus `EffectCommand` enum (`nexus.schema:40`) are exhaustive too; if (and only if) a future phase routes Hetzner through the schema engine, those become the deferral home and will need `HetznerCreateServer` variants. Explicitly out of scope now.\n\n6. **Environment confirmation:** `nix`, `git`, `gopass` are all present (`/run/current-system/sw/bin/nix`, etc.). `std::process::Command` shell-out works (the cloudflare path uses it at `cloudflare_cli.rs:48`).
